## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The nonlinearity can appear in restoring forces, damping, or driving terms, covering models like Duffing, Van der Pol, and parametrically driven oscillators.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external driving)
- Parametrically driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v (time-modulated stiffness)
- Duffing with driving: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced Duffing)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Combined nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (Duffing + Van der Pol)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- Mathieu-Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * cos(c2 * t) + c3 * x**3 + c4 * v (parametric + nonlinear)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — expect only odd powers of x in symmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent linear energy dissipation/injection; terms like x²*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping (Van der Pol type)
- Explicit sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving or parametric excitation
- Product terms x*cos(c*t) indicate parametric resonance where the effective stiffness is modulated in time
- Cubic velocity terms v³ (Rayleigh-type) indicate nonlinear dissipation that limits cycle amplitude
- If acceleration depends only on x (not t or v), the system is conservative and derivable from a potential V(x)
- Sign of the cubic coefficient determines hardening (same sign as linear term) vs softening (opposite sign) spring behavior
- Absence of even powers of x in the restoring force suggests a symmetric double-well or single-well potential
- Mixed terms like x*v suggest velocity-position coupling that can break time-reversal symmetry
